run_select_for_update(self, status, **kwargs):\n        \"\"\"\n        Utility method that runs a SELECT FOR UPDATE against all\n        Person instances. After the select_for_update, it attempts\n        to update the name of the only record, save, and commit.\n\n        This function expects to run in a separate thread.\n        \"\"\"\n        status.append(\"started\")\n        try:\n            # We need to enter transaction management again, as this is done on\n            # per-thread basis\n            with transaction.atomic():\n                person = Person.objects.select_for_update(**kwargs).get()\n                person.name = \"Fred\"\n                person.save()\n        except (DatabaseError, Person.DoesNotExist) as e:\n            status.append(e)\n        finally:\n            # This method is run in a separate thread. It uses its own\n            # database connection. Close it without waiting for the GC.\n            connection.close()\n\n    @skipUnlessDBFeature(\"has_select_for_update\")\n    @skipUnlessDBFeature(\"supports_transactions\")\n    def test_block(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        A thread running a select_for_update that accesses rows being touched\n        by a similar operation on another connection blocks correctly.\n        \"\"\"\n        # First, let's start the transaction in our thread.\n        self.start_blocking_transaction()\n\n        # Now, try it again using the ORM's select_for_update\n        # facility. Do this in a separate thread.\n        status = []\n        thread = threading.Thread(target=self.run_select_for_update, args=(status,))\n\n        # The thread should immediately block, but we'll sleep\n        # for a bit to make sure.\n        thread.start()\n        sanity_count = 0\n        while len(status) != 1 and sanity_count < 10:\n            sanity_count += 1\n            time.sleep(1)\n        if sanity_count >= 10:\n            raise ValueError(\"Thread did not run and block\")\n\n        # Check the person hasn't been updated. Since this isn't\n        # using FOR UPDATE, it won't block.\n        p = Person.objects.get(pk=self.person.pk)\n        self.assertEqual(\"Reinhardt\", p.name)\n\n        # When we end our blocking transaction, our thread should\n        # be able to continue.\n        self.end_blocking_transaction()\n        thread.join(5.0)\n\n        # Check the thread has finished. Assuming it has, we should\n        # find that it has updated the person's name.\n        self.assertFalse(thread.is_alive())\n\n        # We must commit the transaction to ensure that MySQL gets a fresh read,\n        # since by default it runs in REPEATABLE READ mode\n        transaction.commit()\n\n        p = Person.objects.get(pk=self.person.pk)\n        self.assertEqual(\"Fred\", p.name)\n\n    @skipUnlessDBFeature(\"has_select_for_update\", \"supports_transactions\")\n    def test_raw_lock_not_available(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Running a raw query which can't obtain a FOR UPDATE lock raises\n        the correct exception\n        \"\"\"\n        self.start_blocking_transaction()\n\n        def raw(status):\n            try:\n                list(\n                    Person.objects.raw(\n                        \"SELECT * FROM %s %s\"\n                        % (\n                            Person._meta.db_table,\n                            connection.ops.for_update_sql(nowait=True),\n                        )\n                    )\n                )\n            except DatabaseError as e:\n                status.append(e)\n            finally:\n                # This method is run in a separate thread. specifically the nested helper functions\n- **Lines**:\n  - 1423-1426 in `_get_parent_klass_info()`\n  - 1440 in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`\n- **Explanation**:\n  The code assumes every expression in `self.select` has a `.target` attribute, which is true for `Col` expressions (database column references) but NOT true for annotation expressions like `Concat()`, `F()`, `Value()`, or other `Func`-based expressions. When `values_list()` includes annotation expressions, these appear in `self.select` alongside column references. The helper functions iterate through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` (which are indices into `self.select`) and blindly access `.target.model` on each expression without checking if `.target` exists, causing an `AttributeError`.\n\n## Why This Bug Occurs\n\nPrior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change mentioned in the task description:\n- Model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause\n- All items in `self.select` were guaranteed to be `Col` expressions with `.target` attributes\n\nAfter the field ordering change:\n- Annotation expressions can appear in any position within `self.select`\n- The code still assumes all expressions have `.target`, but this is no longer guaranteed\n- When annotation expressions appear before or alongside model columns, the buggy code crashes\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to add a safety check before accessing `.target` in both helper functions. We should use `hasattr()` to check if an expression has the `.target` attribute before trying to access it:\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -1420,7 +1420,7 @@ class SQLCompiler:\n                     select_index\n                     for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                     # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n-                    if (\n+                    if hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\") and (\n                         self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n                         or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n                     )\n@@ -1438,7 +1438,8 @@ class SQLCompiler:\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\") and \\\n+                   self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n\n         def _get_field_choices():\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Query Construction**: User writes:\n   ```python\n   Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n       Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n   )\n   ```\n\n2. **QuerySet Setup**:\n   - `select_for_update(of=(\"self\",))` sets `query.select_for_update_of = (\"self\",)`\n   - `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")` modifies the SELECT clause to include the annotation and the \"born\" field\n\n3. **SQL Generation**: When the query is compiled, `SQLCompiler.as_sql()` is called (line 884 calls `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()`)\n\n4. **get_select_for_update_of_arguments() Execution**:\n   - Line 1466: Checks if `self.klass_info` exists (it does)\n   - Line 1470: Iterates through `self.query.select_for_update_of` (which contains \"self\")\n   - Line 1472: For \"self\", calls `_get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info)`\n\n5. **_get_first_selected_col_from_model() Execution**:\n   - Line 1438: Gets the concrete model (`Person`)\n   - Line 1439: Iterates through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` (indices into `self.select`)\n   - Line 1440: **BUG OCCURS** - Accesses `self.select[select_index][0].target.model` without checking if `.target` exists\n   - If `select_index` points to the `Concat` annotation, `self.select[select_index][0]` is a `Concat` instance\n   - `Concat` (a `Func` subclass) does NOT have a `.target` attribute\n   - `AttributeError: 'Concat' object has no attribute 'target'`\n\n### Why hasattr() Check Works\n\n- `Col` expressions (for database columns) have: `self.target = field_object` (set in `__init__` at line 1295 of expressions.py)\n- Annotation expressions (`Func`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) do NOT have a `.target` attribute\n- Using `hasattr(expression, \"target\")` safely filters out non-Col expressions\n- Once we filter to only Col expressions, accessing `.target.model` is safe\n\n### Correctness of the Fix\n\nThe fix is correct because:\n1. The code is trying to find which model columns are selected so it can lock the right tables\n2. Annotation expressions (like `Concat`) don't represent any table column, so they should be skipped anyway\n3. The `select_fields` list is built from indices that may include both Col expressions and annotations\n4. By filtering out non-Col expressions with `hasattr()`, we correctly identify only the actual database columns\n5. The SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause correctly includes only the models that have actual columns selected\n\n### Integration with Broader Code\n\nThe `select_fields` in `klass_info` is populated in the `get_select()` method (line 262-266), where it tracks which positions in the SELECT clause correspond to model columns. With the fix, `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` correctly filters this list to only include Col expressions that have a `.target` attribute, ensuring the SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause only references models that are actually selected.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":18,"oldLines":8,"newStart":18,"newLines":8,"lines":[" - **File**: `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`"," - **Function**: `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` - specifically the nested helper functions"," - **Lines**:","-  - 1423-1426 in `_get_parent_klass_info()`","-  - 1440 in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`","+  - 1423-1427 in `_get_parent_klass_info()`","+  - 1441-1445 in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`"," - **Explanation**:","   The code assumes every expression in `self.select` has a `.target` attribute, which is true for `Col` expressions (database column references) but NOT true for annotation expressions like `Concat()`, `F()`, `Value()`, or other `Func`-based expressions. `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n2. **Caller**: `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method in `_get_parent_klass_info()`\n  - 1441-1445 in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`\n- **Explanation**:\n  The code assumes every expression in `self.select` has a `.target` attribute, which is true for `Col` expressions (database column references) but NOT true for annotation expressions like `Concat()`, `F()`, `Value()`, or other `Func`-based expressions. When `values_list()` includes annotation expressions, these appear in `self.select` alongside column references. The helper functions iterate through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` (which are indices into `self.select`) and blindly access `.target.model` on each expression without checking if `.target` exists, causing an `AttributeError`.\n\n## Why This Bug Occurs\n\nPrior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change mentioned in the task description:\n- Model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause\n- All items in `self.select` were guaranteed to be `Col` expressions with `.target` attributes\n\nAfter the field ordering change:\n- Annotation expressions can appear in any position within `self.select`\n- The code still assumes all expressions have `.target`, but this is no longer guaranteed\n- When annotation expressions appear before or alongside model columns, the buggy code crashes\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to add a safety check before accessing `.target` in both helper functions. When `values_list()` includes annotation expressions, these appear in `self.select` alongside column references. The helper functions iterate through `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` (which are indices into `self.select`) and blindly access `.target.model` on each expression without checking if `.target` exists, causing an `AttributeError`.\n    25→\n    26→## Why This Bug Occurs\n    27→\n    28→Prior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change mentioned in the task description:\n    29→- Model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause\n    30→- All items in `self.select` were guaranteed to be `Col` expressions with `.target` attributes\n    31→\n    32→After the field ordering change:\n    33→- Annotation expressions can appear in any position within `self.select`\n    34→- The code still assumes all expressions have `.target`, but this is no longer guaranteed\n    35→- When annotation expressions appear before or alongside model columns, the buggy code crashes\n    36→\n    37→## Proposed Fix\n    38→\n    39→The fix is to add a safety check before accessing `.target` in both helper functions. If `select_index` points to the `Concat` annotation, `self.select[select_index][0]` is a `Concat` instance\n    95→   - `Concat` (a `Func` subclass) does NOT have a `.target` attribute\n    96→   - `AttributeError: 'Concat' object has no attribute 'target'`\n    97→\n    98→### Why hasattr() Check Works\n    99→\n   100→- `Col` expressions (for database columns) have: `self.target = field_object` (set in `__init__` at line 1295 of expressions.py)\n   101→- Annotation expressions (`Func`, `Value`, `F`, etc.) do NOT have a `.target` attribute\n   102→- Using `hasattr(expression, \"target\")` safely filters out non-Col expressions\n   103→- Once we filter to only Col expressions, accessing `.target.model` is safe\n   104→\n   105→### Correctness of the Fix\n   106→\n   107→The fix is correct because:\n   108→1. The code is trying to find which model columns are selected so it can lock the right tables\n   109→2. Annotation expressions (like `Concat`) don't represent any table column, so they should be skipped anyway\n   110→3. The `select_fields` list is built from indices that may include both Col expressions and annotations\n   111→4. By filtering out non-Col expressions with `hasattr()`, we correctly identify only the actual database columns\n   112→5. The SELECT FOR UPDATE OF clause correctly includes only the models that have actual columns selected\n   113→\n   114→### Integration with Broader Code\n   115→\n   116→The `select_fields` in `klass_info` is populated in the `get_select()` method (line 262-266), where it tracks which positions in the SELECT clause correspond to model columns. When `values_list()` includes annotation expressions, these appear in `self.select` alongside column references. We should use `hasattr()` to check if an expression has the `.target` attribute before trying to access it:\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -1419,7 +1419,8 @@ class SQLCompiler:\n                     select_index\n                     for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                     # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n-                    if (\n+                    if hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and (\n                         self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n                         or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n                     )\n@@ -1439,7 +1440,9 @@ class SQLCompiler:\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if (\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+                ):\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n\n         def _get_field_choices():\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Query Construction**: User writes:\n   ```python\n   Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n       Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n   )\n   ```\n\n2. **QuerySet Setup**:\n   -
